369.107 Legal recognition of electronic records, electronic signatures, and
@)
@
(3)
4)
electronic contracts.
A record or signature may notbe denied legal effect or enforceability solely because
it is in electronic form.
A contract may not be denied legal effect or enforceability solely because an
electronic record was usedin its formation.
Ifa law requires a record to be in writing, an electronic record satisfies the law.
Ifa law requires a signature, an electronic signature satisfies the law.
Effective; August 1,2000
History: Created 2000 Ky. Acts ch. 301, sec. 7, effective August 1, 2000,

Subjective
Chief Complaint:
VITALS: Weight: 236 Ibs. Height: 68 inches. BMI: 35.9. BP: 138/86. Pulse: 90. Temp: 96.6.
Chronic low back pain
HISTORY OF PRESENT ILLNESS:
Mr. Ruhl is a 56 y/o male (worked in construction now retired) with history of OSA, anxiety,
depression, and ADD who presents for low back pain. The pain started in 2005 without an inciting
event. He has done conservative treatment such as NSAIDs, Tylenol, and heat/ice with minimal
pain relief. He also did physical therapy twice a week for 4 weeks in Sept 2022 but had to stop
because of severe pain. He denies of having any back injections or surgeries in the past. Denies
of having any fever, N/V, constipation, bladder or bowel incontinence.
SYMPTOMATOLOGY:
He presented with low back pain. Timing: Intermittent. Quality: Deep and aching. Location:
Bilateral paravertebral low back pain. Onset: With gradual onset without injury since 2008, with
intermittent, sharp, and shooting. Radiation Quality: Both hips and right lower extremity into toes.
Radiation onset: With worsening gradually since onset. Associated signs and symptoms include
numbness and tingling. Exacerbation with sitting, standing and walking. Relief with lying down
with back pain worse than leg pain. Failed to respond to chiropractic, physical therapy, 2 times
week, September 2022 and medical therapy.
PAST, FAMILY, SOCIAL HISTORY
Previous Tests:
Regular X-rays of upper back and low back.
MRI scan.
Evaluation &Treatment History for Pain
PROVIDER SEEN APPROX. # OF TIMES DURING THE YEARS
Medical history: Chronic bronchitis, COPD, bronchial asthma and sleep apnea syndrome, problems with
concentration, problems with memory, anxiety, depression, bipolar, and attention-deficit disorder/attention

severe neural foraminal or spinal canal encroachment in the lumbar spine.

foraminal encroachment.

We discussed various issues involved in pain management including my impressions, the patient
perceptions, treatment options available, and the development of realistic goals which should
include increased functional capacity, reduced pain, and increased quality of life. We discussed
that pain relief is desirable, however may not be achievable in all cases. We discussed the
process of chronic pain development, its management, and limitations and frustrations of its
management. It was emphasized that a multimodal approach is recommended to inciude positive
attitude and use of relaxation techniques to modify pain behavior, modification of exercise and
activity, procedural interventions when indicated, and limited medication use. We discussed that if
medications are to be continued, they will be administered in a controlled fashion and that the
patient should adhere to the controlled substance agreement of this clinic.
The discussion also included controlled substance management. The patient was counseled
regarding the potential benefits and side effects of opioids, benzodiazepines, and hypnotics, which
include Schedule Il, Ill, IV, V and non-scheduled drugs. The risks described included, but are not
limited to: drowsiness, sedation, dependence, tolerance, addiction, nausea, opioid induced
hyperalgesia, and problems with cognition. They were informed of potential interactions with
various drugs and alcohol and the dangers of operating an automobile while under the influence of
these medications. The risk of falls and fractures was also noted. They received information
regarding potential additional adverse effects of these drugs in the elderly, immunosuppressed,
hormonally deficient, those suffering with sleep apnea syndrome or other respiratory disorders,
and those with cardiovascular disorders. They were informed of the potential for hormonal
disturbances and suppression leading to various other issues such as impotence, sexual
dysfunction, and fatigue. The patient also understands the need to follow the controlled substance
agreement without deviations. The use of any other illicit drugs or medication from others is not
only illegal, but extremely dangerous. The patient should immediately report any type of side
effects and report to the emergency room if major problems ensue, but should not seek additional
fain medications from other providers. The patient expressed understanding and agreement with
this.

Plan
Office Procedures
PROCEDURE: Bilateral L3, L4 medial branch and L5 dorsal ramus blocks under fluoroscopic
guidance.
DIAGNOSIS: Lumbar spondylosis w/o myelopathy or radiculopathy (M47816), Lumbosacral
spondylosis w/o myelopathy or radiculopathy (M47817)
RN: A. Pumphral
RADIOGRAPHIC TECHNOLOGIST: J. Jenkins
INFORMED CONSENT: After reviewing the risks and benefits associated with the procedure. The
informed consent form was signed by the patient.
DESCRIPTION OF PROCEDURE: After informed consent, the patient was transferred to the
operating room. The patient was positioned prone on the fluoroscopy table. Continuous
hemodynamic monitoring was initiated including blood pressure, EKG, and pulse oximetry. The
area of the lumbar spine was prepped with chlorhexidine and draped into a sterile field.
Fluoroscopy was used to identify the location of the bilateral L3 and L4 medial branches, and L5
dorsal ramus at the junctions of the superior articular process and the transverse processes of L3,
L4, LS, and the sacral ala respectively. A 22-gauge, 3.5 spinal needle was slowly inserted at each
level using AP and lateral fluoroscopic imaging. Negative aspiration for blood or CSF was
confirmed. A combination of5 ml bupivacaine 0.25% was injected (1 ml on each level). The
needles were removed, and insertion sites were appropriate. Band-aids were applied.
ASSESSMENT:
The procedure was tolerated well, there were no apparent complications. The patient was taken to
recovery room in stable condition.
Pre-procedure pain: 9/10
Post-procedure pain: 6/10
DISPOSITION: The patient was discharged home with escort.

M47816 Spondylosis w/o myelopathy or radiculopathy, lumbar region
M47817 Spondyls w/o myelopathy or radiculopathy, lumbosacr region

Plan
Office Procedures
PROCEDURE: Bilateral L3 and L4 medial branches and L5 dorsal ramus radiofrequency ablation
under fluoroscopy.
DIAGNOSES: Lumbar spondylosis without myelopathy or radiculopathy (M47816), lumbosacral
spondylosis w/o myelopathy or radiculopathy (M47817).
RN: T. Lipperd.
RADIOGRAPHIC TECHNOLOGIST: F Long
DESCRIPTION OF PROCEDURE: After informed consent, the patient was transferred to the
operating room. The patient was positioned prone on the fluoroscopy table. Continuous
hemodynamic monitoring was initiated including blood pressure and pulse oximetry. The area of
the lumbar spine was prepped with chlorhexidine and draped into a sterile field. Fluoroscopy was
used to identify bilateral L3, L4, and L5 medial branch nerves atthe junctions of the superior
articular process and the transverse processes of L3, L4, L5, and the sacral ala respectively. Skin
anesthesia was achieved using 3 mL of lidocaine 1.0% over the injection sites. An 18-gauge, 100
mm (10 mm active tip) curved RF needle was slowly inserted at each level using AP and lateral
fluoroscopic imaging. Negative aspiration for blood or CSF was confirmed. Motor stimulation at 2
Hz up to 1.5V did not cause any radicular symptoms at any level. Each level was anesthetized
with 1.0 mL of lidocaine 2%. Radiofrequency lesioning was performed for 120 seconds at 80
degrees. Then a solution containing 5 mL of lidocaine 1% was prepared. Then, 1 mL of the
solution was injected at each level. The needles were removed, and insertion sites were
appropriate. Band-aids were applied.

Assessment
Diagnosis
MRI of lumbar spine without contrast done on [DOB-257].
Findings:
The last well-formed disk is designated as L5-S1 for the purposes of this report, and vertebral
bodies were numbered using this convention.
Lumbar vertebral body heights and alignment maintained. The marrow signal in the lumbar spine
is preserved. No evidence of acute fracture, suspicious bone lesion or marrow replacement
process.
The conus medullaris is normal is signal characteristics and morphology. The conus medullaris
terminates at T12-L1. Cauda equina unremarkable.
The visualized portions of the retroperitoneum demonstrate no significant abnormalities. The
paraspinal musculature is grossly unremarkable.
T12-L1: No significant posterior disc bulge or frank herniation. No neural foraminal or spinal canal
encroachment. Bridging osteophyte formation noted anteriorly.
L1-L2: No significant posterior disc bulge of frank herniation. No neural foraminal or spinal
encroachment. Prominent hypertrophic endplate changes are noted anteriorly.
L2-L3: Mild facet arthropathy is noted. No spinal canal encroachment. No left neural foraminal
encroachment. There is a right foraminal disc protrusion that produces moderate right neural
foraminal encroachment.
L3-L4: No significant posterior disc bulge or frank herniation. No neural foraminal or spinal canal
encroachment.
L4-L5: Facet arthropathy and ligamentum flavum hypertrophy noted. No significant posterior disc
bulge or frank herniation. No spinal canal encroachment. There is moderate bilateral neural
foraminal encroachment.
L5-S1: Facet arthropathy is noted. No significant posterior disc bulge or frank herniation. No
spinal canal encroachment. No neural foraminal encroachment.
Remainder of exam unremarkable.
Impression:
1. Multilevel degenerative changes of the lumbar spine are present. There is no evidence of
severe neural foraminal or spinal canal encroachment in the lumbar spine.
2. At L2-L3, there is a right foraminal disc protrusion that produces moderate right neural
foraminal encroachment.
3. Moderate bilateral neural foraminal encroachment related to facet arthropathy is noted L4-
L5.

M47817 Spondyls w/o myelopathy or radiculopathy, lumbosacr region
M5136 Other intervertebral disc degeneration, lumbar region

foraminal or spinal canal encroachment in the lumbar spine.

M62838 Other muscle spasm

Plan
Office Procedures
PROCEDURE: Lumbar epidural injection with steroid under fluoroscopy at L2-3 level.
DIAGNOSIS: M54.16
RN: Pumphrey
RADIOGRAPHIC TECHNOLOGIST: Jenkins
INFORMED CONSENT: After reviewing the risks and benefits associated with the procedure. The informed
consent form was signed bythe patient.
DESCRIPTION OF PROCEDURE: After informed consent, the patient was transferred to the operating
room. The patient was placed in the prone position, and fluoroscopy was used to identify the L2-L3 level.
The lumbar area was prepped with chlorhexidine solution and draped with sterile towels. Sterile technique
was used throughout the procedure. The patient received sedation that was given incrementally to titrate to
effect. At the needle entry point, the skin and subcutaneous tissues was infiltrated with 1.0% lidocaine. A
20-gauge epidural needie was advanced to epidural space, using the loss of resistance technique.
Omnipaque (1 mL) was injected, resulting in good distribution of contrast in the epidural space. No
paresthesia was encountered during needle placement. With the needle in the epidural space, aspiration
was negative for blood or other fluid. Then, a solution of Kenalog 40 mg and normal saline for a total
volume of 5 mL was injected through the epidural needle. The epidural needle was removed, and the
insertion site was appropriate. A band-aid was applied.
ASSESSMENT:
The procedure was tolerated well, there were no apparent complications. The patient was taken
to recovery room in stable condition.
PRE-PROCEDURE PAIN: 8/10
POST-PROCEDURE PAIN: 0/10
DISPOSITION: Patient was discharged home with escort.

Plan
Office Procedures
Surgeon: Xiaoli Wang, MD
Anesthesia: IV sedation.
Pre-Op Diagnosis: Spondylosis without myelopathy or radiculopathy, lumbar region - M47.816
and lumbarsacral region - M47817.
Post-Op Diagnosis: Spondylosis without myelopathy or radiculopathy, lumbar region - M47.816
and lumbarsacral region - M47817.
Procedure Performed: Radiofrequency ablation - Bilateral L3, L4, DR L5.
Method of procedure: The patient was interviewed in the holding area and Risks/Benefits were
discussed, including, but not limited to, the possibility of new or different pain, nerve damage,
bleeding, or infection. All questions were answered. The patient understood and accepted these
risks. Consent was obtained. After an IV was started during pre-procedure work-up, the patient
was brought into the operating room and placed in prone position and prepped with chlorhexidine
and draped in the usual sterile fashion and the procedure was performed using strict aseptic
techniques. The areas to be injected were localized under fluoroscopic guidance and the overlying
soft tissues were infiltrated with 1% lidocaine via a 25-gauge, 1.5-inch needle.
Bilateral L5 dorsal ramus location is identified at the junction of the superior articular process and
sacral ala. Bilateral L3 and L4 medial branch locations are identified at the junction of superior
articular process and transverse process of L3, L4, and L5 vertebral bodies. A 15 cm, 20-gauge
radiofrequency needle with 1 cm active curved tip is introduced to the left side to L3 and L4
medical branch location and L5 dorsal ramus location. Impedance check is performed. Sensory
stimulation at 50 Hz and motor stimulation at 2 Hz are performed at each location. Once the
location is conformed, radiofrequency probes are withdrawn. A 2.5 mL/0.25% bupivacaine is
injected into each needle. The probes are reintroduced. The ablation is performed at 80 degrees
centigrade for 30 seconds. The needles are pulled by half centimeter and turned around 180
degree and ablation is repeated for another 30 seconds. Before the needles are removed, a 0 mg
of Kenalog is injected into each location. Sterile dressing is applied.
Same techniques were applied for the radiofrequency ablation on the other side: Yes
